12.1 Understanding Scalability

Definition and Core Concepts

Scalability is the capability of a system to handle a growing amount of work by adding resources to the system. A truly scalable system maintains or improves its performance characteristics as load increases, without requiring fundamental architectural changes.

The Three Dimensions of Scalability

Scalability vs. Performance

AspectPerformanceScalability
FocusSpeed of individual operationsHandling increased load
MetricResponse time, latencyThroughput, capacity
Question"How fast?""How much?"
OptimizationAlgorithm efficiencyResource multiplication
CeilingLimited by single unitCan grow with resources

Key Insight: A system can be high-performance but not scalable (fast but can't handle more users), or scalable but low-performance (handles many users but slowly).

When to Choose Vertical Scaling

Ideal Scenarios:

  • Small to medium applications
  • Legacy systems difficult to distribute
  • Applications requiring strong consistency
  • Database servers with complex transactions
  • Quick fixes while planning horizontal scaling
  • Predictable, limited growth expectations

Resource Scaling Dimensions:

ResourceScaling ImpactTypical Limits
CPU CoresComputation throughput128-256 cores
RAMIn-memory data, caching4-12 TB
StorageData capacity, I/OPetabytes (SAN)
NetworkBandwidth100+ Gbps
GPUML/Graphics workloads8-16 GPUs
